meta.custom.parentRowIndex to using FieldType.nestedFrames\n */\nexport const migrateFromParentRowIndexToNestedFrames = (frames: DataFrame[] | null) => {\n  const migratedFrames: DataFrame[] = [];\n  const mainFrames = getMainFrames(frames).filter(\n    (frame: DataFrame | undefined): frame is DataFrame => !!frame && frame.length !== 0\n  );\n\n  mainFrames?.forEach((frame) => {\n    const subFrames = frames?.filter((df) => frame.refId === df.refId && df.meta?.custom?.parentRowIndex !== undefined);\n    const subFramesGrouped = groupBy(subFrames, (frame: DataFrame) => frame.meta?.custom?.parentRowIndex);\n    const subFramesByIndex = Object.keys(subFramesGrouped).map((key) => subFramesGrouped[key]);\n    const migratedFrame = { ...frame };\n\n    if (subFrames && subFrames.length > 0) {\n      migratedFrame.fields.push({\n        name: 'nested',\n        type: FieldType.nestedFrames,\n        config: {},\n        values: subFramesByIndex,\n      });\n    }\n    migratedFrames.push(migratedFrame);\n  });\n\n  return migratedFrames;\n};\n\nexport const hasDeprecatedParentRowIndex = (frames: DataFrame[] | null) => {\n  return frames?.some((df) => df.meta?.custom?.parentRowIndex !== undefined);\n};\n\nexport const migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel = (panel: PanelModel<Partial<Options>>) => {\n  if (panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.wrapText !== undefined) {\n    // already migrated\n    return;\n  }\n\n  const legacyDefaultWrapText: boolean | undefined = panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.cellOptions?.wrapText;\n\n  panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map((override) => {\n    if (override.properties) {\n      override.properties = override.properties.flatMap((property) => {\n        if (property.id === 'custom.cellOptions' && property.value && property.value.wrapText !== undefined) {\n          return [\n            { ...property, value: { ...omit(property.value, 'wrapText') } },\n            { id: 'custom.wrapText', value: property.value.wrapText },\n          ];\n        }\n        return [property];\n      });\n    }\n    return override;\n  });\n\n  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom ?? {};\n  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.wrapText = legacyDefaultWrapText;\n  delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.cellOptions?.wrapText;\n\n  return panel;\n};\n\nexport const migrateHiddenFields = (panel: PanelModel<Partial<Options>>) => {\n  panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map((override) => {\n    if (override.properties) {\n      override.properties = override.properties.map((property) => {\n        if (property.id === 'custom.hidden') {\n          return { ...property, id: 'custom.hideFrom.viz' };\n        }\n        return property;\n      });\n    }\n    return override;\n  });\n\n  return panel;\n};\n\ninterface LegacyTableFooterOptions {\n  show: boolean;\n  reducer: string[];\n  fields?: string[];\n  countRows?: boolean;\n  enablePagination?: boolean;\n}\n\nexport const migrateFooterV2 = (panel: PanelModel<Options>) => {\n  if (panel.options && 'footer' in panel.options) {\n    // we need to cast the footer to the old type to work with it here.\n    // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/consistent-type-assertions\n    const oldFooter = panel.options.footer as LegacyTableFooterOptions;\n\n    if (oldFooter.show) {\n      const reducers = oldFooter.reducer;\n\n      panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = {\n        ...panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom,\n        footer: {\n          reducers: reducers,\n        },\n      };\n\n      if (oldFooter.countRows && reducers[0] === 'count') {\n        panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.footer.reducers = ['countAll'];\n      } else if (oldFooter.fields && oldFooter.fields.length > 1) {\n        delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.footer;\n\n        // Fields is an array of field names, so push a byNames matcher\n        // on with the matched reducer.\n        panel.fieldConfig.overrides.push({\n          matcher: {\n            id: FieldMatcherID.byNames,\n            options: {\n              mode: ByNamesMatcherMode.include,\n              names: oldFooter.fields,\n            },\n          },\n          properties: [{ id: 'custom.footer.reducers', value: reducers }],\n        });\n      } else if (oldFooter.fields && oldFooter.fields.length === 1) {\n        delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.footer;\n\n        // Single field, so we can use a byName matcher\n        panel.fieldConfig.overrides.push({\n          matcher: {\n            id: FieldMatcherID.byName,\n            options: oldFooter.fields[0],\n          },\n          properties: [{ id: 'custom.footer.reducers', value: reducers }],\n        });\n      }\n    }\n\n {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01SYjwfRfNm1fa8esdsH9iwQ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the table panel migrations. Let me understand the issue:\n\n1. The problem is that field override configuration is silently dropped during dashboard import\n2. Dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom` are affected\n3. Dashboards with explicit custom config are unaffected\n\nLooking at the migrations code, I can see several migration functions:\n- `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel` (line 306-334)\n- `migrateHiddenFields` (line 336-350)\n- `migrateFooterV2` (line 360-413)\n\nThe issue appears to be in how these functions handle `panel.fieldConfig`. Let me look at the `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel` function more carefully:\n\n```typescript\nexport const migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel = (panel: PanelModel<Partial<Options>>) => {\n  if (panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.wrapText !== undefined) {\n    // already migrated\n    return;\n  }\n\n  const legacyDefaultWrapText: boolean | undefined = panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.cellOptions?.wrapText;\n\n  panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map((override) => {\n    // ...\n  });\n\n  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom ?? {};\n  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.wrapText = legacyDefaultWrapText;\n  delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.cellOptions?.wrapText;\n\n  return panel;\n};\n```\n\nWait, looking at line 314:\n\n```typescript\npanel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map((override) => {\n```\n\nIf `panel.fieldConfig` is undefined or if `panel.fieldConfig.overrides` is undefined, this will fail! The function assumes `panel.fieldConfig.overrides` exists, but it might not if the dashboard doesn't have explicit `defaults.custom`.\n\n\nThe same pattern repeats in `migrateHiddenFields` - it directly accesses `panel.fieldConfig.overrides` without null checks. And `migrateFooterV2` appears to have similar issues with unsafe property access on potentially undefined objects. The migration handler calls three functions—`WrapToFieldLevel`, `migrateHiddenFields`, and `migrateFooterV2`—but none of them validate that `panel.fieldConfig` exists before accessing its properties. In real dashboards where `fieldConfig` was never initialized, attempting to access `.overrides` or `.defaults.custom` on an undefined object would cause silent failures or runtime errors. The task description says:\n\"The bug only affects dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` was not explicitly set in the saved dashboard JSON.\"\n\nAnd the migration functions like `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel`, `migrateHiddenFields`, and `migrateFooterV2` all directly access `panel.fieldConfig` and its nested properties without checking if they exist.\n\nLet me check if there's a missing null check. Looking at `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel` again:\n\n```typescript\nexport const migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel = (panel: PanelModel<Partial<Options>>) => {\n  if (panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.wrapText !== undefined) {\n    // already migrated\n    return;  }\n\n  const legacyDefaultWrapText: boolean | undefined = panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.cellOptions?.wrapText;\n\n  panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map((override) => {\n    // ...\n  });\n\n  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom ?? {};\n  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.wrapText = legacyDefaultWrapText;\n  delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.cellOptions?.wrapText;\n\n  return panel;\n};\n```\n\nThe issue is at line 314: `panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map(...)`\n\nThis line ASSUMES that `panel.fieldConfig` is not null/undefined. But what if it is? Let me check if there's an early return that prevents reaching this line...\n\nLooking at the code:- Line 307 checks if `panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.wrapText !== undefined`\n\n\n- If that condition is true, the function returns early at line 309\n- But when it's undefined (the typical case for dashboards without explicit custom config), execution continues to line 314\n\nThe optional chaining in that first check means it safely evaluates to false if `panel.fieldConfig` doesn't exist, so no error there. However, once past that check, the code directly accesses `panel.fieldConfig.overrides` without verifying `panel.fieldConfig` itself exists. If `fieldConfig` is undefined, this will throw an error when trying to access its `overrides` property.\n\nThe solution involves adding a guard clause before that access—either initializing `fieldConfig` with default values if it's missing, or returning early if `overrides` doesn't exist. Looking at the `restoreModel` method in the PanelModel constructor, properties from the persisted model are copied directly, which means `fieldConfig` could legitimately be undefined if it wasn't explicitly set.\n\nThe core issue is that the migration functions assume `fieldConfig` is always properly structured, but older dashboards or certain save states might have undefined or incomplete `fieldConfig` objects. When `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is not explicitly set in the saved dashboard JSON, the migration code attempts to access properties on potentially undefined objects, causing failures that are not properly handled.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe regression is caused by **three table panel migration functions** that directly access `panel.fieldConfig` and its nested properties without checking if they exist:\n\n1. **`migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel()`** (migrations.ts:306-334)\n   - Line 314: `panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map(...)`\n   - Assumes `panel.fieldConfig` is initialized with an `overrides` array\n   - Missing check: Does not verify `panel.fieldConfig` is not null/undefined before access\n\n2. **`migrateHiddenFields()`** (migrations.ts:336-350)\n   - Line 337: `panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map(...)`\n   - Identical issue: Direct access without null/undefined checks\n   - Can fail with \"Cannot read property 'overrides' of undefined\"\n\n3. **`migrateFooterV2()`** (migrations.ts:360-413)\n   - Line 369-370: `panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = { ...panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom, ... }`\n   - Line 383, 397: `panel.fieldConfig.overrides.push(...)`\n   - Missing checks before accessing `defaults.custom` and `overrides`\n\n## Evidence\n\n### File: `/workspace/public/app/plugins/panel/table/migrations.ts`\n\n**Problem Code - `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel` (lines 306-334):**\n```typescript\nexport const migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel = (panel: PanelModel<Partial<Options>>) => {\n  if (panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.wrapText !== undefined) {\n    // already migrated\n    return;\n  }\n\n  const legacyDefaultWrapText: boolean | undefined = panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.cellOptions?.wrapText;\n\n  // BUG: No check for panel.fieldConfig existence before accessing .overrides\n  panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map((override) => {\n    // ...\n  });\n\n  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom ?? {};\n  // ...\n};\n```\n\n**Problem Code - `migrateHiddenFields` (lines 336-350):**\n```typescript\nexport const migrateHiddenFields = (panel: PanelModel<Partial<Options>>) => {\n  // BUG: Direct access without null/undefined check\n  panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map((override) => {\n    // ...\n  });\n  return panel;\n};\n```\n\n**Problem Code - `migrateFooterV2` (lines 360-413):**\n```typescript\nexport const migrateFooterV2 = (panel: PanelModel<Options>) => {\n  if (panel.options && 'footer' in panel.options) {\n    const oldFooter = panel.options.footer as LegacyTableFooterOptions;\n\n    if (oldFooter.show) {\n      // BUG: Assumes fieldConfig.defaults.custom exists\n      panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = {\n        ...panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom,\n        footer: { reducers: reducers },\n      };\n\n      // BUG: Assumes fieldConfig.overrides exists and is an array\n      panel.fieldConfig.overrides.push({\n        // ...\n      });\n    }\n  }\n};\n```\n\n### File: `/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`\n\n**Schema Version 38 Migration (lines 644-674):**\n```typescript\nif (oldVersion < 38 && finalTargetVersion >= 38) {\n  panelUpgrades.push((panel: PanelModel) => {\n    if (panel.type === 'table' && panel.fieldConfig !== undefined) {\n      const displayMode = panel.fieldConfig.defaults?.custom?.displayMode;\n\n      // Only processes if displayMode exists\n      if (displayMode !== undefined) {\n        // Migration logic\n      }\n    }\n    return panel;\n  });\n}\n```\n\n**Issue:** The condition checks `panel.fieldConfig !== undefined` but doesn't validate the structure of `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`. Dashboards without explicit custom config skip this migration entirely.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **Panel Table Plugin:**\n   - Package: `/public/app/plugins/panel/table/`\n   - Files: `migrations.ts`, `module.tsx`\n   - Functions: `tableMigrationHandler`, `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel`, `migrateHiddenFields`, `migrateFooterV2`\n\n2. **Dashboard State Management:**\n   - Package: `/public/app/features/dashboard/state/`\n   - File: `DashboardMigrator.ts` (schema version 38)\n   - File: `PanelModel.ts` (plugin lifecycle - `pluginLoaded` method)\n\n3. **Dashboard Model:**\n   - File: `DashboardModel.ts`\n   - Instantiates panels and triggers schema migrations\n\n## Why Dashboards with Explicit `defaults.custom` Are Unaffected\n\nWhen a dashboard has explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` configuration in the saved JSON:\n\n1. The PanelModel is created with the full structure: `fieldConfig: { defaults: { custom: { ... } }, overrides: [...] }`\n2. All three migration functions can safely access `panel.fieldConfig.overrides` because the property exists\n3. Optional chaining checks like `panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.displayMode` succeed\n4. The migrations complete successfully and field overrides are preserved\n\n## Why Dashboards Without Explicit `defaults.custom` Fail\n\nWhen a dashboard has `fieldConfig` but no explicit `defaults.custom`:\n\n1. Saved JSON: `fieldConfig: { defaults: {}, overrides: [] }` (no custom property)\n2. During import, PanelModel initializes fieldConfig via `defaultsDeep`, but structure might be inconsistent\n3. `tableMigrationHandler` is invoked during plugin load\n4. `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel`, `migrateHiddenFields`, and `migrateFooterV2` attempt to access `panel.fieldConfig.overrides` or `panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n5. If `panel.fieldConfig` is undefined or malformed, these functions fail silently\n6. Field override configuration is lost because the migration never completes\n7. Table panels render without column formatting (widths, alignment, display modes)\n\n## Conditional Logic Failure\n\nThe migration chain fails due to the following sequence:\n\n1. **PanelModel Creation:** `defaultsDeep()` initializes fieldConfig structure\n2. **Schema v38 Migration:** Skipped if `panel.fieldConfig === undefined` (line 646)\n3. **Plugin Load:** `pluginLoaded()` method invokes `tableMigrationHandler`\n4. **Table Migrations:** Directly access nested properties without checks:\n   - Assumes `panel.fieldConfig !== null && panel.fieldConfig !== undefined`\n   - Assumes `panel.fieldConfig.overrides` is always an array\n   - Assumes `panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom` exists (or safely creates it)\n5. **Failure Point:** If fieldConfig is malformed, accessing `.overrides` throws an error\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n1. **Defensive Initialization:** Add null/undefined checks before accessing `fieldConfig` properties in all three migration functions.\n\n2. **Specific Fixes Required:**\n   - In `migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel`: Check `if (!panel.fieldConfig?.overrides)` before the map operation\n   - In `migrateHiddenFields`: Check `if (!panel.fieldConfig?.overrides)` before the map operation\n   - In `migrateFooterV2`: Check `if (!panel.fieldConfig?.defaults)` before accessing `defaults.custom`\n   - In `migrateFooterV2`: Check `if (!panel.fieldConfig?.overrides)` before calling push\n\n3. **Fallback Initialization:** Ensure `fieldConfig` has the expected structure before migrations run:\n   ```typescript\n   if (!panel.fieldConfig) {\n     panel.fieldConfig = { defaults: {}, overrides: [] };\n   }\n   if (!panel.fieldConfig.defaults) {\n     panel.fieldConfig.defaults = {};\n   }\n   if (!Array.isArray(panel.fieldConfig.overrides)) {\n     panel.fieldConfig.overrides = [];\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Early Return Pattern:** Implement safe return paths:\n   ```typescript\n   if (!panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {\n     return panel;\n   }\n   ```\n\n### Root Issue\nMissing defensive programming in table migration functions that assume `fieldConfig` structure without validation.
